This hotel will rip you off without even thinking about it.Bottom Line is.....I'm not looking for super luxury, I just want a place to stay on New years since I booked it, but when a business screws up, I'd expect them to take responsibility and AT LEAST not be dismissive. <Author>sambeauxjangles
<Content>Charming and nice... for the price Disclaimer: We only stayed one night, so I can't speak to all of the amenities. First off, the valet was prompt and took our car as soon as we pulled up. The desk clerk when we checked in was friendly, but seemed preoccupied with something else. However, the attitude is typical of every hotel we've stayed at from the Monteleone to the Royal Sonesta, and others. I hate to say it, but southern hospitality seems to have vanished from the local hotel business.Our room was nice, looked just like the photos, and pretty clean. The wireless internet worked great (you have to pay the $6.95 whether you use it or not).Remember, this is an old warehouse and some of the rustic characteristics gives it its charm. If you want fancy, stay at the Royal Sonesta or Hotel Monteleone.We paid only $57 plus taxes  the mandatory $6.95 phone/internet charge, and it came with free valet parking. I would stay again for a similar price, but wouldn't pay much more than that.

<Content>"Nightmare on Tchoupitoulas Street" My family and I contacted the property after seeing the ad on Orbitz, the lady who booked the property agreed to match Orbitz.com advertisement. We book a room with two double beds to accomodate 4 people. When we arrived to the hotel, we waited on the bellman, but to our surprise, my parents who are seniors and myself had to tug our heavy luggage upstairs. There was no escort to help, staff was not even friendly. We were also notified that it was $26/day to valet park. We were tired from our long trip and went to our room in hopes of bathing and getting to sleep. We got up to the floor and it was a huge maze in the hallway. I almost slipped on the hardwood floor, it was slippery for some reason right at the doorway. The room that we got had no windows. There were not enough towels in the bathroom. The sink in the bathroom was obviously old and appeared to be coming off the wall. The toliet was leaking from the lid and there was water on the floor from the leaky toliet bowl. The toliet ran all night. Staff were informed of the situation about the room and had a non chalant attitude. The shower curtain had mildew, as if they have not changed the curtains in awhile. ****Note, there is a Walmart less than five minutes from the hotel where they can buy shower curtains.**** During the night, the air condition went out. The next morning, we woke up to begin our journey. As advertised, there was no continental breakfast, but there was coffee. We waited about twenty minutes for the one valet on duty for the morning. The valet told us to retain our ticket to get our car when we come back. We left the hotel for the day, and came back that night. To our amazement, we were told that the parking lot was full, so we could not valet park. We were told that it is not the hotel's responsibilty to hold a spot for the car. We attempted to explain that we paid for valet parking for the two nights we would be there. The desk clerk stated that the hotel will reimburse our money, but the lot had benn full since 5:00pm that evening and we returned after 8:30 pm that night. We immediately went accross the street to park in the lot that was $25 for a 24 hour period. We asked for a manager, but was told there was no manager on duty. The only people available was the man who valet park the cars, and a lady who sat behind her desk not attentive to the guest's needs. When we got back to our room, the air condition was fixed, but water was now leaking from the vents. The only good thing that came of the hotel stay was that it was in a good location. I am a native of the city and was attempting to bring revenue back home, because I live out of the city. I travel to New Orleans frequently, but not recommend anyone who is coming to the city to this hotel. Service is poor: there is noone to greet guest. There is no manager on duty, at least that is what guest is told. Housekeeping is awful! If one is in a crunch and just have to be at this hotel, park at the lot across the street after parking for the night. At least you don't have to wait 20 minutes to get your car. You can walk straight to your car. This was an unbelieveable experience. I am glad I know the city, because this would be a more horrible experience for a first time tourist.

<Author>ATXCruiser
<Content>A totally utilitarian hotel During the Summer months (Low Season) many hotels in New Orleans give discounts. On a tourism webpage I found this hotel as advertising $99 for 2 nights plus free valet. It worked out perfect for me and my girlfriend as we were going to just walk around and party a bit. The catch is that you have to call the 800 number on the tourism website and let them book. Don't forget to verify the free parking, ask them to put a note on the reservation about it. I waited a couple days and called the hotel directly for reservation verification. All was fine and they verified free parking. We arrived and staff was pleasant, bill was around $115 because of tax but parking was free. The room is totally utilitarian, four walls, no view, hot water, and cold AC. It was very noisy because hard wood floors and 15ft ceilings do carry the slightest sound. Bed was kinda gross but we brought our own sheets and when it comes down to it we really didn't care after a night out on Bourbon Street. I recommend this place for college kids and low maintenance people. The price was right and we slept soundly.

<Content>Unfortunate Disappointment My husband and I decided to save some money and experience staying at an independent hotel, rather than a large chain. We thought the hotel pictures and many hotel reviews would lead to a pleasant and affordable stay. We figured since we are city explorers, we wouldnt be spending much time there anyways. I called the hotel directly and reserved a room for three nights after seeing the Summer Sizzler promotion the hotel was offering. We requested a room with a view of the front street and 1 king size bed, which was noted when making the reservation. Upon our arrival at 10:30pm, the hotel stated that our reservation had been cancelled. We were dumbfounded at how this could be possible. The staff did nothing to accommodate our stay until we insisted that they find us a room. The manager was not available to speak to. We finally got a room that was a maze to get to. The uneven floors did not bother us, neither did the maze...it was quite comedic and gave us some lighthearted fun. The room was ok, although a bit dusty on the floors, a dinky window in the corner of the room without a view and ability to be a natural light source...in addition to not one, but TWO kingsize beds. Throughout our stay, we had to call to have the safe replaced/fixed and ended up with a dirty iron, which left black tar on my husband's dress shirt for the suit he brought to wear to the wedding we were in town for. The tar melted on the sleeve of he shirt, and he was unable to wear it. The housekeeping service did not give us clean coffee cups or refresh our coffee supply. It was headache after headache, and we do not plan on staying at this hotel if we return to New Orleans. We did mention the shirt/iron incident to the manager when we were leaving the hotel and after breifly making excuses that they were not responsible, he agreed to have it laundered and sent back home to us. Just today (a month and a half after our stay) we have not received the shirt of a phone call from the manager. I called him today and reminded him of the incident, so he is now crediting our credit card for the expense of the shirt. If you want some piece of mind and enjoy your stay, I suggest looking elsewhere and finding a hotel/flight bundle on expedia or similar site...we learned the hard way! (p.s. Do NOT go to Mother's for food either. The hotel suggested it, and it was absolutely horrible. go to the art district, a wonderful spot called Cafe Beignet...it's definately worth the walk!)

<Author>NOLA126
<Content>So Pleasantly Surprised I had to book 3 rooms for a group coming in to town and it happened to also be Jazzfest weekend. Everything in town was booked or rediculously priced. Although the Ambassador was still high priced (just for this peak weekend) if was a good location and deal for what we needed. After booking I started to read the reviews of the hotel and got very worried about our stay. I couldn't cancel our reservations and later found out that when you booked through a third party (hotels.com, expedia, etc) your bed preference was noted, but not guaranteed. People complained about rude staff, dirty rooms, uncomfortable beds, etc. I spoke directly with someone at the hotel who said they were under new management and made a note of my concerns and my need for two beds in each room. It was absolutley smooth sailing from then on out. The staff knew my needs exactly when I checked in, and were beyond helpful in getting rooms for our group that were close together. The roms were beautiful and very clean. We didn't have a window with a view, but no hotel guarantees that. I think that most of the people who post bad comments about this hotel did not do enough research on it prior to booking. We knew going in that there was no room service, there was a $7 mandatory fee that covered phone calls and internet usage, and that not all rooms had outside views. Who spends a lot of time in their hotel in New Orleans anyway? Our rooms were very clean, the beds were very comfortable, if I wanted to spend all day there, it would have been perfect, too. The bar downstairs is great, and has doors that open up right to the street. I think that if you do your research and look for the amenities you want, you can always find the right hotel. The Ambassador is definitely taking their review seriously and has worked to fix many of the previous problems posted in people's reviews. I also heard from those reviews that the walls were paper thin but never experienced a problem with that either. I think as long as you communicate your needs to the hotel staff they are more than happy to meet them. They were very kind and available. My only needs improvement would be the Valet. Sometimes you couldn't find a valet for over 15 minutes, but the front desk attendant was more than happy to get our keys for us, as we could see where our car was parked. Also, a bellman or two might be a nice addition to the hotel services. Overall it was a great stay, we walked everywhere we needed to go, and only two blocks from Harrahs! I would stay here again, especially because when it isn't a holiday weekend, the hotel price is a great deal.  
<Date>May 7, 2008

<Author>yojaaax
<Content>screwed While we didn't get to stay at the ambassador, I do think anyone planning to should hear my story. My wife booked a room on Mar. 2nd for 4 nights, May 1st thru 4th. This was our 20th anniversary, and we were going to celebrate it at Jazzfest. We got a rate of $169 per night, bought airfare, jazzfest tickets, and made restaurant reservations. On Monday, April 28th, I came home from work about 6:30 pm and found my wife hysterically crying on the sofa. Listen to the message on the phone, she sobbed. It was a personality-less male voice saying our reservations had been cancelled because our credit card was denied, and if there was a problem, call them. My wife had tried, but was told the same thing. It turns out we had been the victim of identity theft and our credit limit on that particular card had been reduced, unbeknownst to us, via a credit report from Experian. Needless to say, once the facts were known, our original credit line was reinstated - the very next day. The ambassador refused to let us use another card, and said they had no more rooms, anyway. They didn't even aknowledge that this was not our fault and could have been solved easily. They just GAVE our room away, for $369 now, by the way, without the slightest bit of sensitivity or concern. We wound up getting one of the last hotel rooms in New Orleans, for alot more money, and still hope to have a good vacation. Despite repeated attempts to contact management, no one has returned my phone calls. I did get emotional in my initial phone call to the hotel, and I have to believe that's one reason. I yelled, so now it's my fault, I guess their thinking goes. This did not have to turn out this way. A simple  call us back, there's a problem with your card could have remedied it. Identity theft is commonplace these days, and that should have been a factor to be considered..  Did I mention they got $369 for our $169 room? Hmmmmmm.................. makes you wonder.

<Author>bzdchris
<Content>Better than I expected! After seeing the reviews of this hotel here and at hotels.com, I had a lot of misgivings. But we went ahead and stayed there for French Quarter Festival and it all worked out great. The room was charming, with two comfortable queen beds, plenty of pillows, a desk and an armoire for the TV and our clothes. It was relatively clean, and the staff was good about making our beds and supplying us with towels. The only glitch was coordinating four key cards, but the staff was good about that too (although they should really check IDs before resetting key cards). We found out on our last day that we could have requested a refrigerator in the room, so there are amenities that are not apparent and the staff is not necessarily forthcoming. There were no unexpected charges (we did not bring or rent a car), and had no problem getting to the festival stages or the French Quarter either by cab or foot. All in all, it was convenient and nice. All four of us in our party would definitely stay there again.

<Author>zintastikcowbell
<Content>Hello? Customer Service?? Like the city of New Orleans, itself, on the surface, the hotel seems great, but if you look a bit closer, you'll discover it's a rip-off.The architecture is very charming, and the price seems right... until they tell you that you'll be paying PER PERSON for parking (not per car), plus $7 just in case you will use the phone (how many local people do they expect you to call?) and/or wireless internet. The Parking Lot is a few blocks away (someone will escort you there), and is enclosed by a chain-link fence. They only serve coffee, seemingly, on Saturdays (maybe Sundays), and I guess they had pastries, because I saw butter and jam, but they didn't replenish those when they replenished the coffee.The bedspreads are stained (we called one the placenta bag, cuz it looked like it had blood stains on the underside), and have holes in them, as do some of the mattress covers. The bathtub is very slippery to step into, and was oddly curved (not flat) on the bottom, so that standing seemed awkward. Also, after a few days, the AC proved finicky/unpredictable, and the windows were totally sealed shut.The staff (especailly the desk clerks) are, indeed, notoriously rude. When we asked for extra blankets (the AC air was hitting two friends in the face), apparently they only keep one or two extras on hand. My friend called the desk with a different question, and they were snippy. Then on the final day, when checking out, the desk clerk got very confrontational with my friend, when there was a discrepency in some of the charges. At one point, the desk clerk said something like if you keep talking to me like that, I WILL charge you an extra day for parking. The bell hop tried to smooth things over, but it made for a terrible last day of our trip, when we were already tired and cranky, to begin with.Now six of us were staying in a room designed for four (we brought an air mattress), and were there for five days, for a conference. Perhaps if a party of two wanted to take a cheap trip to NOLA for a brief weekend, things wouldn't be so bad. The location is pretty good, though be prepared for a lot of walking on uneven streets throughout the city.Overall, though, I would rather shell out a few extra bucks for a nicer experience.

<Author>cjval
<Content>If you are looking for old world charm, stay at the Ambassador I had stayed at this hotel in 2000 and found it a great location and value at that time. I returned to NOLA in December 2006 and was looking for a place to bring a small group. I took a look at this property again and liked what I saw. It is walking distance to the French Quarter and and an easy streetcar ride to the Garden District. There are good restaurants within walking distance.The hotel is a former coffee warehouse, so don't expect all the rooms to be the same! The exposed brick and high ceilings really add to the charm of this hotel.I was a bit hesitant after reading some of the reiews, but found my fears were totally groundless The rooms were clean, comfortable, quiet and in reasonably good repair ( some rooms were still being remodeled, painted etc.) The linens were fresh and clean and appeared new. and the service was outstanding.. The hotel staff was very responisve and friendly. and did everyhting they could to make us feel welcome and cared for. I took about 30 people and we booked 18 rooms for 4 days. No one complained. and everyone raved about the event.The only negative issues were with the contracted concierge service, and I did make that known to the hotel management. You are better off to make your own arrangements.All in ll it was a greeat experience and I would not hesitate to recommend this hotel. I plan to stay there whenever I visit NOLA.

<Content>Quaint little hotel just off the beaten path We stayed here during Mardi Gras which is a hectic time for hotels in New Orleans. Our room was very quaint with hardwood floors and brick walls. The bedspreads were a little threadbare, but I don't usually use them anyway. The only complaint was the bathroom floor which had dirt and hair (not mine) in the corners. The customer service turns what would be a much more pleasant hotel into one that is much less pleasant. The valet parking feels like you are parking a car in someone's lawn during a big football game. Maybe your car will have a spot when you come back and maybe not, and it is so casual on whether they will retrieve your car or not. The great thing about this hotel is that someone could take this hotel, and make it a fantastic place. It is in a great location and has great bones! It is just not there yet...

<Content>Excellent, no frills room Recently took a spur of the moment trip to NOLA from Houston, and found the Ambassador online via an iPhone in a Starbucks on the way. I didn't book online or in advance at all, but they still helped us get a single room for the online special price. <Author>Kjr05001
<Content>Below Average Central Business District Hotel This is the second hotel we stayed in New Orleans (the other one was the Maison Dupuy). In the future we would certainly pick the Maison Dupuy over the Ambassador. It is a convenient location for the central business district, Harrah's Casino and the Riverwalk, but it is a long walk to the French Quarter. There are no convenience stores within easy walk and the hotel does not have any toiletries for sale or complimentary. The Hotel claims to have a breakfast restaurant but it consists of scrambled eggs and waffles. The price is way too high for the quality. The restaurant is nice for lunch. There is sporadic concierge service and the front desk is at best unhelpful at worst rude. The beds are uncomfortable, the room is small and claustrophobic. The TV is VERY small. There is no sitting area and each room is equipped with only 2 poor quality pillows. The maid service is severely lacking. They pretty much made our bed and changed the towels. No new cups were provided even though the cups were clearly used. The coffee was not refilled, the floors were not cleaned. All in all there are many better hotels in NO, this one is not worth the money.

<Author>MNtraveler1399
<Content>Good NOLA hotel Let me start off by saying I am not a picky person about hotels. I travel very frequently and look for the best deal I can find for the money. I stayed at this hotel with a group for Mardi Gras last year. I am from the area originally so travel here at least once a year. I have stayed at many hotels including Prince Conti, The Hilton at Riverplace, Holiday Inn in the Quarter and a few places outside the city in Meridian. I enjoyed our stay at the Ambassador. Payed only $56 a night from Priceline during Mardi Gras week, which if you have ever been during this time, you know is a steal. The front desk was friendly. We were given a fairly large room on the first floor, two double beds. My other travelling companions were on the second floor in an interior room. It had no windows, which I didn't even notice, but was a large room. Both rooms were cleaned each day to our satisfaction. Location is two blocks north of Harrod's, if you like casinos this one is very close. Side note - there is a McAllister's deli in the casino, if you have never been try the BLT. They are open fairly late, midnight at the time. It was a good 15 minute walk to the Quarter. All of my group was able to easily walk the distance, even late at night it was safe. You can expect to walk a lot in this city, so 15 minutes to Jackson Square is nothing compared to what you will walk for the rest of the day.The hotel is older, which is one of the reasons I booked it, for the ambience. Those that normally book in newer hotel chains with sterile environments may be put off.One thing that may be my misunderstanding, but I thought they offered a free breakfast. We went to the restaurant on our last morning but breakfast was not free. In fact it was pretty expensive for you got, so we skipped it.All in all very nice!  
<Date>Dec 28, 2007

<Author>Lynoria
<Content>Being a local, take my advice and stay away from this one! My husband and I are native New Orleanians who now live North of the Big Easy. To do our part in rebuilding OUR city, the one we were born and raised in, we make it a point to spend at least one night a month in the French Quarter. As we like to call it--Play Tourist. We buy from the local shop owners and eat in the local restaurants, all in an effert to help support NOLA post Katrina.We usually try to stay at a different hotel each month so that we can experience The Quarter from all angles. We'll this is one of the angles we wished we'd missed. This place is a dump for lack of a better word. We had a king sized room that the a/c-heater didn't work. The needle was missing off the thermostat--so you had no idea what temperature it was nor did the thermostat-so you had to turn it on fan on and turn it off yourself when you got too hot or cold. Auto was not an option.Getting up in the middle of the night to turn on/off the ac/heater was not something I was fond of but a neccessity both nights we stayed there.The second problem, the walls are soooo thin you can hear everything the occupants in the next room are saying. It's especially annoying when they came in drunk at 3am and start arguing about who's going to win the football game the next day. When we knocked on the wall to get them to quiet down, they just knocked back and said take that. We then called the front desk. Someone finally went to their room and told them to keep it down. That worked for about 5 minutes. Finally, one of the guys in the room told the other guy he wanted to get some rest and shut the[--] up! We mentioned it to the desk clerk the next day and she offered us another room. We felt it was to much trouble for just one more night.The desk clerks and bellman/valets were friendly and helpful. They knew we were locals and did seem to appreciate we were spending our money/tips there.We got free parking which was the only good thing in the 2 days we stayed. However, we took a cab back and forth from the hotel to the French Quarter (it was too far to walk) to the tune of $20 a day...so did we really save a lot?To sum it up, this dingy old coffee warehouse a.k.a hotel is in need of a severe face lift. Don't expect too much and you won't be disappointed.

<Author>CaliforniaJim
<Content>Lots of character, a real bargain We've enjoyed several stays at the Ambassador in the last couple of years. It's a coffee warehouse converted into a hotel; lots of character in the best meaning of the term. It's far enough from the French Quarter to be quiet, but still within easy walking distance. There are several excellent restaurants nearby. We've recommended it to friends, who have also enjoyed their stay there. I consider it one of the real lodging bargains in New Orleans.

<Author>ndstrukt
<Content>Not bad at all I was somewhat hesitant to book a room at this hotel due to the numerous negative reviews on tripadvisor, but I was on a budget, and the hotel's website was running a special ($109 for a 2-night Friday/Saturday stay with free parking), so I decided to take a chance. I requested a room in the Lafayette Wing and wound up in Room 280 on the 2nd floor. The room was quite large, with hardwood floors, marble tile and freshly-painted pale yellow walls in the bathroom, vaulted ceilings, and a large window overlooking the street. I have stayed in dozens of hotels in the French Quarter/N.O. business district, and this was better than most. However, there were 3 negatives: 1) a small bit of mildew in the bathtub. But hey, I wasn't in New Orleans to soak in the tub anyway. 2) Ceilings and walls are EXTREMELY thin. My advice is to either bring earplugs, or request a room on the top floor. You can hear people's chairs above you scraping across the wood floors, and the noise in the hallway can be so loud at times (not from rowdy people, just from general movement, doors shutting, cleaning staff, etc.) 3) Some of the front desk staff needs some customer service training, or they need to hire more professional people to represent their hotel. I am fairly young, and was dressed in casual attire when I checked in, and the young woman at the front desk treated me as such, saying, Wassup? Did they tell you about the $6.95 resort fee? I responded yes and she replied, Good, then I don't gotta explain it. Then she chuckled and said, I'm sorry... [-], I'm just tired. Not good.

<Author>heinertx
<Content>Average for New Orleans My wife and I along with my parents stayed at the Ambassador Hotel May 23-26. After reading the previous reviews my wife called to make sure we had rooms with windows. We were on the first floor so that ended up not really mattering as we were on the first floor so if you opened the blinds ello?side street and smokers/passers by. My basic summary is that for the price the hotel was fine. Sure, it could be cleaner and better lit. (They seem to be switching to compact fluorescents which is fine but the bulbs they chose just are not bright enough in the rooms) The attempt at re-caulking the tub area needs a special mention. It seems to me that who ever did the work (it was the same in my parent room too) was the most inept caulker on the planet. It was a mess. The floors in the rooms were dusty. On the plus side the street noise was negligible. I can say that about some of the people using the ice/snack/drink machines. (drinking seems to make everyone louder) Tip-not only ask for windows but for a room away from the snack area. The beds were firm, AC worked and the ceiling fan was nice to have. The hotel location is great (warehouse district) if you are going to visit areas outside the Quarter. Walking to the WW II museum, Aquarium of the Americas, Casino (very close) or the Quarter itself are easy and cabs (used United) came quickly when called. The staff was fine and the porter/valet was helpful with directions and the like. The PC in the lobby is handy too. The attached bar was standard. The only glitch staff wise was when we left the regular porter/valet was on break or maybe lunch and the guy standing in was incompetent. We had checked out and checked our bags to run around the city one more time before heading to the airport. When we gave the stand-in guy our luggage check tickets he seemed befuddled when attempting to match the ticket numbers to the bags. He tried to give us two wrong bags and not some of our own. When we got to the airport we realized we still had one bag too many. My wife called the hotel and was transferred to the manager and we worked it out by leaving it at one of airlines back check-in stands to be picked up later. The manager was very appreciative and offered to comp some rooms the next time we stayed with them. That was a nice offer.

<Author>ToyInBabeLand
<Content>Impressed after reading bad reviews... I was extremely concerned about staying at this hotel after reading all the negative reviews. My friends who came along depended on me when it came to organizing the trip and I was so afraid that they would be dissapointed. I had no idea what the reviews looked like until two days prior to our trip, I had already reserved the room and feared looking for a different hotel at the last minute would be risky. We arrived at the hotel, I was still nervous but felt ease when they reacted to the great location and the attractive lobby. They were happy and told me so far I had made a good choice. The front desk person was friendly and checked us in quickly. The Vallet guy seemed moody but neevr directed anything toward us. Our car was parked in a gated area, which I did verify by going to my car. A huge relief after reading that the cars were parked in a dark unattended alley. I assure you that it's gated. Sturdy iron gates. As we went to our room, my friends were again very pleased with the style. I inspected the room for mold and dirt, but found nothing like that, I did howeevr find a pair of crusty mens socks hanging from a sink pipe and my friend found a pair of flip flops under the bed. The bathroom was clean and the shower looked safe. The water pressure was a little low, but the temperature was always perfect. The pillolws were fine and the blankets were nice, not shabby as I had seen on a review. There were no windows wich confused our bodies as we always thought is was still night time, we had to set the alarm clock to know it was day time. There are rooms with windows, you just have to be lucky I guess. It wasn't so bad though. The only complaint I have is that you can hear evrything through the walls, people are inconsiderate of this and walk through the hall ways talking and laughing loud. The people upstairs from us seemed to walk around their room excessively, I don't know how someone can walk in such a small room that much. It was a distraction, especially at 5 a.m. when I was trying to sleep. My drunk travel buddies never even noticed. The employees were friendly but rarely smiled, I was smiled at once by a housekeeper who greeted me as I walked toward my room. Overall the location is wonderful, and it felt very safe. I may stay again, the price was great. If you plan on getting sleep there you may want to stay somewhere more quiet. I believe it's all hit or miss.. Maybe you'll have a wonderful stay, maybe you wont... It's a gamble.

<Author>jengoSantaBarbaraCA
<Content>My stay was good, but took alot of work to make it that way First time staying here. Came for Jazzfest. I booked my stay through Priceline, which I will NEVER, EVER do again! The rates were the same if you booked directly through the hotel ( $140 per night plus taxes  parking) and they offer 1/2 off on parking as an incentive. Priceline categorizes Ambassador as 3-star...which I STRONGLY disagree with. This is not 3-star...1.5 at best. After I booked on priceline, I looked it up on tripadvisor  freaked out at the negetive reviews...and there were many. I've stayed in N.O many, many times, but never in this area. A few days prior to arrival- I called Ambassadors reservations dept. and spoke with abby. I expressed my concers about the hotel  told her of the negetive reviews. She did her best to quickly assure me that they have made alot of recent changes and improvments to the hotel(staffing  remodeling) and that she was confident I would enjoy my stay. She offered me 50% off on valet parking ( $30 per day down to $15 in the hotel's parking lot), and noted my request for a room in the lafayette wing. She also waved thier $6.75 a day resort fee- without asking. I had the sense, that she'd been through this routine many times before...damage control. Anyway, when I arrived my room was ready ( 11:30 am), so I was happy with that...The front desk clerk sped through the check-in , so I had to verify the notes on the discounts were there, Before checking in...this was important later at check-out, when the clerk was trying to charge me for all these things...we straightened it out, but just added a bit of stress, that was totally preventable! I was happy with the appearance of the lobby ( the hotel manager was present in the lobby, dressed nicely and greeting guest- 1st day only), which was nice. My room in the lafayette wing was fine. Actually better than expected. The beds were antique style  a bit saggy, and the bathroom was clean enough, but I shower was a little moldy, so I wore sandals. Overall, I was satisfied, because I was there for Jazzfest  wouldn't be in the room much, except to crash  shower. I declined room service during my stayed ( felt safer about my personal belongings that way) as the room attendants I encountered didn't seem to care much about thier professional conduct around guests ( loud  pretty unfriendly). I took full advantage of the free internet on thier lobby computer, for purchasing tickets for evening shows, checking bank statements, checking-in for return flight, printing maps, etc. ...this was a very usefull amenity during Jazzfest! The location of the hotel was great! The Arts  Wherehouse district is directly across from the convention center and immedietly surrounded by numerous large chain hotels which have restaurants and bars/lounges you can utilize. Very easy walk to Sheraton on Canal to catch JF express. Mother's restaturant is across the street! Bonus! Howlin' Wolf is about 5 blocks away- easy walk. Emerils restaurant is 2 blocks away. We felt pretty safe walking at night ( during JF) because there were always people out  about on Tchoupatoulas. Didn't have any issues with valet or our car...they said they have an enclosed parking lot now, which I didn't verify, but I beleive, because they told me they would walk me over if I needed to retrieve stuff from my car. There is also a pay parking lot directly across the street, which I beleive was cheaper. Very easy access to the freeway.The hotel has a restuarant/bar, which looked nice for appetizers  martini's, but I never made it there. Overall, my stay was fine for JF. I don't know if I would stay there again, because I feel like I had to do alot of extra work to ensure my stay be satisfactory. Which I don't feel you should have to do at a 3-star property. There was a couple of women who I saw at the front desk arguing with the clerk. They had booked a Year in advance and had apparently only stayed in the lafayette wing before, because thier room this time was in terrible condition and NOTHING like what they stayed in before, nor did it look anything like any of thier friends rooms. They were very upset..but the front desk didn't move them or offer anything else. SO- I will VERY likely look for other accomodations in the same area, which was great! Not sure if I would want to press my luck at the Ambassador.

<Author>vicchickBrooklyn
<Content>Fix the water pressure or we won't come back We were prepared to cut this hotel a break. Some of the complaints seemed a little petty in light of what a bargain this place is. You've got to keep things in perspective. Plus the location is phenomonal. We stayed for Jazzfest and it's very close to the unofficial and far better bus to the fairgrounds and it's close to French Quarter and it's right around the corner from Cafe Adelaide a wonderful Brennan restaurant. But then I went to take a shower. The water pressure is sad. In the morning it's barely a trickle and in the evening it's just limp. I need real showers. The hotel knows they have a problem. It's not just our room. I don't know that they're doing anything about it.Not having a decent shower is a deal breaker. Everything else about the hotel is adequate. It's not a place to impress. I would have recommended it for budget conscience travelers save that one fatal downfall.And yes, the mandatory $7 bucks a day for unlimited phone service is a gouge. it encouraged us to make calls like mad to get even.

<Author>JNTexas
<Content>Better than expected After reading the horrific reviews about this hotel, I was very nervous about staying here. However, I found both the staff and the room very accommodating. We booked the room through the website, but later saw that if you called the hotel 1-800 reservation number you would receive a 2 for 1 special and free parking. Since we were 4 guys on a mini-vacation, we elected to call and book four separate rooms. We received a MUCH better deal than if we booked through a discount online vendor such as Travelocity. Make sure and ask for a room in the Lafayette wing. These rooms were the ones they advertise on the website, not the Bates Motel, mold infested, windowless rooms I have read about here on Travel Advisor. The room was small, but comfortable and clean, with hardwood floors and a single Queen sized bed. One note, the elevator bank to this wing is not the one located adjacent to the lobby. You have to walk around a small hallway maze located on the left side of the lobby which takes you around to the Lafayette wing. Just ask the front desk people or any employee and they will help you. The showers take a while to heat up so don hop in right away or you will be screaming at the top of your lungs. All four of us had this issue. Overall, it was a good bargain hotel, with a good location. The W hotel is right across the street (Whiskey bar is great by the way) and you can see the entrance to Harrah Casino sign from the front door of the hotel. It is about a 10 minute walk from Bourbon Street. Cheers.

<Author>italianaeorgogliosa
<Content>Always reliable - best deal in town We travel to New Orleans quite often. we often stay at the Ambassador because we think it has the best quality/price ratio in New Orleans. Many other more snobbish hotel in this city do not offer the same accomodations.The location is ideal, within walking distance to everything. The service is very good. The staff at the front desk is excellent, they are always helpful and go out of their way to accomodate our needs. Parking is the best. Usually it is free (depending on how you book your room) and if you don't want to valet park the car, the parking lot across the street is a good alternative. The restaurant next door is nothing to write home about but there is plenty of great restaurants in the area. Our room was spacious with confortable beds, decently clean. I would highly recommend this hotel if you want charm and are not too snob.

<Author>Cotton_Farmer_Clay
<Content>Best keep secret in New Orleans Hotels Just returned from a wonderful cruise and mini vacation in New Orleans. If you are looking for a hotel that not only is pleaseing to the eye but truelly transports you back to the old south this is the one for you. Beautifully decorated with breath taking historical details I was truelly amazed by the beautiful high ceilings and traditional decor as well as brick and plaster walls (straight from the sugar warehouse days!!). My room had hard wood floors and 12' high ceilings. This was completely different from any hotel I have ever stayed at.  Its location is perfect, parking right across the street and within walking distance from all the best food, entertainment and gaming. French quarter was just down the road and the casino could be seen from the hotel as well as the riverwalk. If you have any questions Mr. Smith, the manager, personally gave SUPER pointers on were to eat ( Moms and The Coffee Pot were superb), what to do and how to get there. The Hotel provided us with maps and directions. I was truelly impressed with the wonderful Old southern charm of not only the Hotel but the employees within it. This is a MUST see for all that plan on a stress free vacation. I have never had a hotel go so far out of their way to make my stay enjoyable. Only regret was that i had to leave to catch my cruise.

<Author>Silverfish16
<Content>A great hotel in a great location! My daughter and I stayed at the Ambassador this past weekend so we could go to the Sugar Bowl (Geaux Tigers!). The Ambassador was the perfect hotel in the perfect location. We had to book a room with one king sized bed as that was all that was available to us over the hotel website. David Smith, the Rooms Division Manager, learned of this and moved us to a double room, much better. The room we moved into had a problem with the door lock but that was handled very promptly by the hotel maintenance department. They too are deserved of a compliment. The work was done quickly and the men that performed the work were very friendly and efficient in their work.The hotel is full of local New Orleans character, the hard wood floors, the brick walls, the mazelike hallways and the staff. If you want a little taste of the city, stay here. I understand that some of the hotel has been renovated and another part not but I suspect the plans are in place to take care of this.This hotel is also in a fabulous location. Since we were there for the game (at the Superdome) the walk was about 10 blocks but the hotel is also only a short walk from the French Quarter, and an even shorter walk to the River Walk Mall and the casino. This hotel has a great location without some of the inconveniences of the French Quarter hotels. It does not have the all night traffic of Bourbon Street outside. Great hotel, great location, count me in for another stay.

<Author>The_Crazy_Brazilian
<Content>Not the horror show some reviews lead us to believe After finding out the 3-star hotel I've booked thru priceline was the Ambassador I confess I was worried with the possibility of being assigned one of the windowless rooms so many people complained about. Guess what? I got one of those and it was not that bad. The building is an old warehouse that was converted into a hotel and has a number of internal rooms with windows opening to to small internal patios. Granted, you need to keep your curtains closed all the time to have some privacy, but the air conditioning works fine and the exhaust system is good so, short of a view you will not notice that your window opens to an internal hall. This is a budget hotel and if you keep that in mind you will not be disappointed. My only complaint is about the dragon lady from hell at the front desk - avoid the light brunette with glasses and you will be fine ;).

<Author>FSUAmanda
<Content>Character, Comfort and Charm! I was skeptical when I saw the great summer rates for the Ambassador Hotel, but I knew that I'd found a great deal when I checked in! The Ambassador Hotel in New Orleans is not only in a great, safe location, but it has character, comfort and charm. I love it here. The lobby is classy, the staff is friendly and the furnishings are rich and comfortable. It's actually like staying in a bed and breakfast in an old home, but it happens to be a great hotel in a great location. There's also a great restaurant that serves breakfast, lunch and dinner. Harrah's Casino (for those who like to gamble or eat at buffets), the W New Orleans (for a little swankier taste) and Lulu's Restaurant (casual, sandwiches, drinks) are all within walking distance. It's also within walking distance of the French Quarter. It's very hot down here, though, so you'll enjoy coming back to your air conditioned room!

<Author>pineapp
<Content>For the $ - acceptable. It was by error that I got lowered my star rating on Priceline that I ended up with The Ambassador. I was a little concerned by the reviews here, but decided to keep my reservation and see what I found. I have stayed at nearly all the hotels in the CBD of New Orleans. I like the location of the Ambassador. My room was very large, with TWO king size beds. I especially like the hard wood floors. Other than some noise from an adjoining stairway, my room was quiet. No window to speak of - a small opening looking into a brick wall. I was disappointed that there was no regular coffee for the in suite service - only decaf. There were chucks of marble missing from the vanity and shower surround. The exhaust fan in the bathroom was VERY loud at start up, but did get quieter. The water pressure has much to be desired! The hallways appeared unkept. The front desk people were very friendly and helpful with all requests including receiving faxes, etc. The Ambassador COULD be a great property with a little TLC - but for $59, I really could not complain.

<Author>DaLumZ
<Content>ask for a room with a window facing harrah's We most certainly can understand the mixed reviews here. Our family of 5 booked 2 rooms. There were no rooms on the same floor, so we were separated by one floor - which was no problem. My husband  I took the room on the 3rd floor  the rest of the family had the 4th floor. Upon entering our room, we weren't totally turned off, however the room was very dark  dingy. My husband went to open the blinds  the view was the hotel hallway leading to other rooms. There wasn't sufficient lighting in this room at all. It was dinnertime, so we just dropped off our things  met the rest of the family on the 4th floor. What a total difference!! Their room was so much nicer, with big windows facing Harrah's, a ceiling fan, nice bathroom with lots of counterspace, a closet with sliding mirrored doors, etc. Total opposite of what we just checked into. Later that night, we went back to our dingy room  discovered there were 2 large tiles fronting the toilet bowl that were completely loose. We also discovered that the toilet didn't flush. The sink in the bathroom had several cracks in it. I called the front desk to ask for a room change. After about 10 minutes of being on hold, she told me to come  pick up the keys to the new room. The next morning we asked the housekeeper for 2 extra pillows  were left 2 pillow cases (no pillows). Called the front desk when we got back that afternoon to request the same thing. 30 minutes later, still no pillows. Called the front desk (again) to request pillows  10 minutes later - FINALLY we got what we requested! They charge $4.95/day for wireless internet, local  continental U.S. calls. We were in a room on the back side of the hotel  the wireless signal was so weak - we'd connect for 30 - 45 seconds, then get disconnected. I brought this up with the hotel  they adjusted the charges at check out, so that was nice.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great place - great staff- great location- great rates We just completed a four night stay at the Ambassador hotel in New Orleans. I am shocked at the negative reviews on this page - the hotel was clean, the staff were overly helpful and polite, customer service was evident in every interaction we had with the staff. Walter at the front desk, Oscar, the bellman, Raquel and others went out of their way to assist us during our stay. Directions to attractions, extra coffee in our room, and prompt service describe the staff. The hotel is a conversion from a coffee wharehouse built in the mid 1800's - It has been converted beautifully and the decor is quaint, not overdone or stuffy. We did not eat at the restaurant but heard from others that the food was good. The 4.95 charge added to the bill was for unlimited long distance and DSL for the intranet. It is charged to each room - I have paid as much as 20.00 a night for DSL in other locations - so the 4.95 was a very slight charge for this service - and to make unlimited free long distance calls from the room... This was a first for me - a great service and a very nominal fee. It is unfortunate that others posting reviews have left such negative comments - It seems impossible to me that they could be referring to the same hotel in which we just lodged.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't let the negative reviews fool you My frends and I spent two nights at the Ambassador this past weekend, and found the hotel to be clean, the front desk very friendly...especially Walter, who was a great help to us and very nice. If you're looking for a spotless new hotel with all the bells and whistles, then this place isn't for you. This place has a history, it's a coffee warehouse that was renovated and has character. There are more renovations are going on, and if you have a problem with that, then you might be better elsewhere. But we didn't find them to be troublesome, we were prepared by reading their website, etc. Plus, we weren't there to sit in our hotel all day, we were out and about. This is a good spot with a good location for lots of things you'll want to do and see in New Orleans...they are more than happy to give you suggestions on shortcuts, make phone calls for your shuttle, and all in a timely manner.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel with Character This was the third hotel in New Orleans that we stayed in in a two week period. It was both the cheapest and our favorite. (We also stayed in the Iberville Suites and the Amerihost).The Ambassador is located in the Warehouse District which is the burgeoning Arts / Business District. Though outside of the normal tourist venue, it is quite nice. It is in walking distance to the Quarter. The hotel is in an old warehouse building that has been converted. The rooms feel like tiny loft apartments. High ceilings, hardwood floors, some exposed brick, decorated with interesting accents such as custom iron pieces. When we were there, the hotel was in the process of being remodeled, so some painting was going on in the hallway and they had yet to replace some of the older carpet.Our only complaint was that the sevice was slow, though we found this to be true at all three hotels we stayed in, even the luxury hotel that cost significantly more. Our conclusion, service in New Orleans will be good, but much slower than the faster paced cities of the West or East coast. Also, the restuarnt was Mexican, so you will not be able to order the generic New Orleans fare (jambalaya, red beans  rice...) with room service. We found the food to be both good and resonable. Overall, we had a great stay at the Ambassador and will stay there again.  
<Date>Jun 28, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Ambassador was great! I visited New Orleans recently to attend a national conference. The conference hotel was pricey and I was staying with 2 other colleagues. We decided that we could afford to go early and stay later than the conference if we could book somewhere more affordable. We found the Ambassador. They were great. I missed the flight with my colleagues and they arrived ahead of time and were well taken care of despite the fact that I had the reservations in my name. They were able to take their luggage and unpack and rest while they waited for me. The room looked exactly like the photos on the web. They were much larger than other hotel rooms. The rooms were clean, cool, and comfortable. Not everything, matched and the walls needed a little painting here and there, but who cares when you just want a nice comfortable place to sleep. The staff was friendly and everyone quickly got to know us and helped us with all of our needs. I would definitely recommend this hotel to others and I would stay there again. It is only a little more than a block away from the trolley/riverside and a hop skip and a jump to Bourbon Street. The cantina next door was a great place to grab a drink too! There were a number of European guests staying the same time as us and it was fun to see where everyone was from.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Hotel in a Great Location I gave an average rating because what else would you expect from a low rate hotel. Having traveled all through Europe, I found the Ambassador Hotel to be very similar to those I stayed in oversees, quaint, comfortable and clean. The location was great. You are better off going to a flagged hotel and spend the extra money to be pampered. If you are looking for a place just to store your bags and enjoy what New Orleans has to offer at a reasonable rate then stay at the Ambassador Hotel.

Since it was booked through Expedia.com, there was nothing that they would do except take off the mandatory $4.95 phone surcharge (although that was pretty cool, since all local and continental long distance charges were included in that).It was a big disappointment from start to finish.

<Author>RiversideGator
<Content>A Good Deal In A Good Location I stayed at the Ambassador Hotel from April 6-10 and was worried having read some of the previous reviews. I must say that I was pleasantly surprised. The hotel is not a Ritz Carlton, but you shouldnt expect this if paying on average $100 per night or less. I would say the hotel is comparable to a Holiday Inn or other 3 star hotel. The positives: Close to French Quarter without being in all that mess and a block and a half from Harrah's Casino. The negatives: Rooms fairly small and paint job in our room looked as if they began to repaint and stopped halfway. Still, our room was very clean, the sheets and towels were changed daily and the bathroom was restocked with towels, soap and shampoo every day. Even the furniture was tasteful. The bottom line is this was a good deal and those who complain either (a) are complainers generally or (b) normally stay at much nicer places.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't let the bad reviews scare you away!! My co-worker and I were booked into the Ambassador by our employer for a convention this April. We were excited because this hotel sounded quaint and unique but the bad reviews really worried us. Every staff member at the hotel was very helpful. The desk clerks were friendly. We had housekeeping service every day which included fresh towels!! We had plenty of hot water and good water pressure. The only night that was noisy was the last night we were there but it didn't keep me awake. New Orleans is a night town and that's when the fun is. It's an easy walk to the French Quarter and the convention center and it's only a couple of blocks to the trolley and city bus stops. This hotel was built in an old coffee warehouse so it has some old things but we certainly enjoyed our stay and would stay there again!! Beware of the concierge because they want you to book your tours the monute you check in. Don't!! There's lots of free tours and you'll want to explore so that you know what you really want to do.

<Content>Great old hotel in a great location I stayed at the Ambassador a week ago and had a wonderful time! I did have one of the infamous windowless rooms (the hotel is an old renovated warehouse of sorts) but the ambiance of the authentic New Orleans decor (exposed brick, high ceilings, wood floors) made it almost seem like being in old France. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Decent Hotel but Staff Needs Some Improvement. My girlfriend and I stayed here for a week in Feb, 2004. It is definitely a no-frills environment but I didn't find it as awful as most reviewers seem to have.The room was adequate in size, the bed was comfortable and the bathroom was a tight squeeze but clean. We also had no problems with water pressure and/or temperature. Everything worked properly...the TV, lights, fans, etc. We did have one of the infamous non-views though...our window opened onto some sort of air shaft.There was a somewhat disconcerting episode with a fire alarm one night though. The alarm sounded sometime after 1am and the fire department arrrived on site. Guests just sort of wandered into the halls and eventually down to the lobby. The hotel staff never made any sort of announcement that all was OK or that there should be an evacuation. There was no information given at all. They were all standing near the front doors or out in the street by the firefighting vehicles. I (somewhat jokingly) compared it to the crew of a cruise liner abandoning ship and leaving the passengers behind. Luckily it was a false alarm.In terms of customer service the staff was adequate...the bellman was particulary good. We had housekeeping service every day unlike some reviewers. But the fire alarm incident cast a huge shadow of doubt over the staff's ability to handle any sort of emergency.This is a decent hotel to use if you are on a tight budget and/or don't plan on spending a lot of time in your room.

<Content>Our favorite hotel in New Orleans My wife and I first stayed here on spur of the moment visit to New Orleans. I was a bit concerned after I had booked my room at the Ambassador for a convention-- I read on line reviews and thought that I'd made a mistake.I've stayed at many hotels all over the world, and the Ambassador isn't the best I've stayed at, but it sure isn't the worst.Some of the issues other people have had, and what I actually found:Noise: Yep. It's noisy. It is a renovated warehouse, so soundproofing isn't built into it. Bring ear plugs. I do no matter where I stay. Dirty: Lobby and hall areas are under renovation, carpets are dirty, but in the process of being replaced. Room was fine. Sticky floors isn't due to dirt or yucky stuff, but a high laquer poly finish-- walking on it with bare feet and a slightly humid climate will make it feel sticky. Trust me, it's not strawberry jelly ;)House keeping: House keeping came every day. There is a sign on the sink and bed explaining the need to conserve water-- if you want the bed changed every day-- don't leave the little sign on the bed. You want clean towels, throw the dirty ones on the floor. Hey, I don't change my sheets every day at home, I don't need them changed every day at a hotel. Water conservation is important-- use the towels more than once.Crappy service: When I checked in I was told there was a DSL line in my room, with the ethernet cable. I got to the room, no cable. I called down to the desk and got someone that told me I had to buy my own, which I thought was bull. Next day I visited the desk in person, spoke with Josh and Raelynn (I think the names are right) and they hunted one up for me-- no charge. Hotel staff informed me that they are in the process of going wireless in the whole hotel. Currently lobby has wireless internet-- worked fine.Remote control: Changed the channels, but didn't turn off the tv or control the volume. I don't care, I can get off of my lazy butt-- plus I'm not really into tv anyway. Come on, this is New Orleans-- get out and DO something!In summary-- The Ambassador is a mid-priced hotel, in a conveinent location. It is nothing fancy, but is a good place to lay your head at night. I'd like to see a comfortable chair in the room, as well as a good reading light. Bring and ethernet cable if you want to get on line, and be aware that the in room safe is small, my 12 Powerbook barely fit in it. If you want a hotel that his totally consistant, try a Motel 6. I want something a little different, and The Ambassador fits the bill just fine.  
<Date>Oct 13, 2004

<Content>Good experience at the Ambassador I wasn't sure what to expect after reading the poor reviews. My husband and I stayed there for one weeknight in July and am glad to report we had a good experience. (It's definitely not the place to stay if you are looking for a corporate hotel.) This unique building once served as an office building for a coffee company. For this it has certain character reflected in its structure and decor. Our experience lent good service, a good rate, comfortable room and bedding, and best of all, great a/c. (Note-within the surrouding area, it's my opinion that overall retail customer service is not at its best and not what I'm used to. I would be more inclined to think it's due to the native social culture rather than the merchant. ) Don't forget this hotel is within good walking distance of Bourbon St, the Riverwalk, and Harrah's casino.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Has potential, but missed the mark. We booked over the internet and got a great deal, under $50.The lobby was interesting, but the wall behind the front desk looked like some kids tried to cover old wallpaper with black paint and texture. The elevator was a little scary. When you look down you can see the basement all lit up with spooky lamps and all the trash that falls. The walls were clean in the halls, but the carpets seemed a bit stained and unclean. The room was nice, once we could get the door open. We were on the third floor in 325. Two big windows and wood floors. Our safety lock and deadbolt barely worked and only if you slammed the door very hard. There was a hole in the floor by the window, termite damage. We blocked it with a piece of luggage so our children wouldn't get hurt. There was mold on the beautiful exposed brick, but the linens were very clean. More termite damage was evident in the morning when one of our sons moved the curtain back and a baseboard crumbled. No one was hurt though, yet! Later that evening one son cut his foot badly on an exposed nailhead on the old wood floor. I went to the desk to ask for a first aid kit and no one knew anything. I got two bandages and was immediately dismissed. Not very compassionate. Our water pressure was fine, but there was mold in the bathroom. I loved the tile and wrought iron in the bathroom though. Just a little more work and the hotel could have some serious charm. We had no problems with housekeeping or valet. We didn't use the restaurant, but it looked more like a bar from what we could see. Probably won't get back to this place any time soon, but I hope they can fix it up.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Didn't need the valium... I took a valium after reading earlier reviews of this hotel, i.e. the shower was like someone urinating on me when I had already booked the package -- I even tried to cancel the trip. The hotel turned out to be great -- clean streamlined room with hardwoood floors and exposed brick walls, nice bathroom -- no plumbing problems. I've previously stayed at the Sheraton on Canal, the Fairmont, and the W in the French Quarter (now closed) and the Ambassador is my favorite. Well, that's a lie, I loved that W French Quarter but since that one closed, I'd stay at the Ambassador again -- esp. for $59 and that's even the hotel's website price. There seems to be a big range in room quality so ask for another if you don't like what they give you -- saw one at the end of the hall that looked like it had old, bright green carpet. Also peeked into a gorgeous room with huge windows, two double beds and which was at least 3 times larger than my single king. Don't stay here if you're really dazzled by bright floral wallpaper and matching flower pattern bedspreads, and furniture with faux gold trimming a la Louis the XVI -- book a room at the Fairmont, instead. This hotel is the anti Laura Ashley aesthetic -- clean neutral lines with an urban feel.

After we went searching for the rooms (the layout of the hotel is extremely confusing) we returned to the lobby, but she was not there, so we went and packed up our things. 15 minutes when we returned, she told us she had called security on us since we had taken so long. <Content>Great location Spent February 17, 2004 at the Ambassador Hotel in New Orleans.Had little trouble finding the hotel but parking was something different. Ended up parking across the street in a lot that charged almost $15 for the night. We checked into room 234 and immediately had problems with the room. The bed was unmade and dirty towels were on the floor. I contacted the front desk and we were moved to another room, 317, which was awesome! The room had a living room and then a bedroom with a nice bath. Although there were no outside windows, it was great! The hotel is having a problem with the city over water pressure so call before booking a room. Once the water pressure is solved, this will be a great place to stay when visiting the Big Easy!It is located about two blocks from Harrah's casino, several blocks from the D-day museum, and several blocks from the quarter. This hotel isn't completely perfect but it does have a bar and a restarurant. I would definately recommend this hotel to my friends who enjoy traveling!  
<Date>Jan 25, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great bargain On a recent trip to New Orleans, my boyfriend and I decided to stay at the Ambassador hotel. The price was so good that I was a little apprehensive about the quality of the hotel. When we got there we were taken care of by polite staff and quickly got into our room. The room was smaller than a average hotel room, but the very high ceilings along with the hardwood floors really made the room. One side of the room was all windows, which overlooked a sidestreet. This was one of the things I liked most about the room. We had lots of towels, good water pressure, and it was all clean. The bar and restaurant in the hotel was impressive, too. A very nice bartender and a little two man band made it all that much nicer. And for the price we got the room at, we were able to go splurge on a dinner at Nola's, which was not far down the road. I would recommend this hotel to anyone looking for a good hotel for a good price.  
<Date>Jan 25, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hated It!! I'm originally from NOLA and this was a trip back home. This hotel sounded intriguing, and yes, it's a block from Mother's, and that's a real treat.Problems: mouse in companion's room; roaches in ours. Enough said!! This is New Orleans, but really, there should be varmit control.Booked through AAA--they got the rate wrong and we had to pay double. Still waiting for the adjustment, which may never come. It's been four months now.Not only would I never go back to this place, I would avoid NOLA. No dinner was under $100, and even the neighborhood places were at least $35 per person. Bourbon Street is pathetic, the city is close to Third World no matter how much new building they do. We were right to leave. The only saving grace is Cafe du Monde and the magnificent biegnets (and Mother's, of course).Save your money and avoid this hotel at all costs.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Horrible Stay!! We stayed at the Ambassador Hotel during the New Years holiday and the experience was horrible!! When we arrived at the hotel, we were not given the room we requested. We booked a room for 4 people but were given a room with only 1 bed. They told us that the hotel was full and could only bring ONE rollaway twin bed for our other TWO guests. We asked the staff how this mistake could happen and they blamed it on our internet booking agency. They claimed to only have a reservation for 2 people and they also said this has happened a lot from this internet booking agency. We were told that we could get another room in the morning, but nothing could be done that night. We asked for a copy of our reservation information, but were told that it was confidential between the hotel and internet booking agency. After a long discussion with the rude manager, we were given a different room because the room we were in could not even fit rollaway beds. We had to drag all of our stuff (ourselves, no help offered) to a room with a smaller bed so 2 rollaway beds could be put in. Everything in the room was pushed in one corner and made our room extremely cramped. In the morning we inquired about our new room and were told that it wouldn't be ready until later in the day, but we still had to check out of our current room before noon. Obviously, they didn't mind inconveniencing us so they could have the room ready for the next guest. We had to drag all of our stuff back to the lobby so they could store it until our new room was ready. We were roomless for over 2 hours! Finally, our room was ready and had everything we asked for in our reservation, but this never should've happened in the first place.I have dealt the same internet booking agency on other occasions and never had any problems. I feel like I was lied to by the hotel staff and would never stay there again!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>You get what you pay for We got a great deal but it seems you get what you pay for. The people at the front desk hassled us when we checked in and when we checked out. We made a reservation with a deposit through a third party internet firm. They told us they didn't have a room when we tried to check in. When we argued about it they suddenly found a room and acted like they were doing us a favor. The room had NO water pressure - not enough to take a shower. Everyone we talked to had the same problem. To be fair, they did agree to give us a different room the second night which was much better. (on the first floor) When we checked out they did not want to give us credit for the deposit we had paid. We argued and the manager finally approved it. The location is good and the price is good but next time I will pay a little more and enjoy decent service and a shower.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A nice surprise Right before my trip to New Orleans, I read the reviews that were here and I was scared. After arriving to the hotel, I was okay. It is very cozy and comfortable. The staff was very nice and if we needed anything, they brought it up then. The room has high ceilings which also make the room look a lot bigger. It was said the single rooms are very tiny and I disagree. I saw the larger room and the single was just as cozy. If you are going to the city, save your money to spend on things like Emeril's and Harrah's and stay at the Ambassador.
